## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology (biological population growth)
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of population change dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, placing it squarely in population dynamics. Classical models express dP/dt as density-dependent functions of P, often with additional time dependence representing environmental fluctuations or changing carrying capacity.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted growth when resources are unlimited)
- Logistic growth (differential form): dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (saturating growth with carrying capacity K = c0/c1)
- Theta-logistic (Richards) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (P / c1)**c2) (asymmetric sigmoid growth with adjustable shape parameter c2)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (sigmoid growth with skewed inflection, often used for tumor or organism growth)
- von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth where metabolic rate scales as a power of body mass, typical c1=2/3 or 3/4)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (cubic growth with a low-density threshold below which population declines)
- Logistic with time-varying carrying capacity (linear trend): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * t)) (environmental change linearly altering the maximum sustainable population)
- Logistic with constant-effort harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P (population with proportional removal, e.g., fishing or hunting)
- Logistic with Michaelis-Menten harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / c1) - c2 * P / (c3 + P) (saturating harvest effort, e.g., predator functional response)
- Periodic carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - P / (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal oscillations in resource availability)
- Density-dependent growth with time-varying intrinsic rate: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - P / c3) (periodic variation in growth rate due to environmental cycles)
- Generalized Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P / c1 - 1) * (1 - P / c2) (intermediate form with distinct thresholds for positive growth)
- Power-law density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P**c3 (general form combining anabolism and catabolism scaling allometrically)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-P linear growth → near P≈0, dP/dt should be approximately proportional to P (exponential growth) if there is no Allee effect; absence of linear P term or negative linear P term suggests Allee threshold.
- Saturation and carrying capacity → a negative quadratic term in P (like -c*P^2) or division by (1 + c*P) indicates density-dependent regulation that caps the population.
- Sigmoid inflection point shift → replacing (1 - P/K) by (1 - (P/K)^θ) or using log(K/P) shifts the inflection point from 0.5K to other fractions, creating asymmetry in the S-curve.
- Time-dependent parameters → presence of additive or multiplicative terms involving t (e.g., c1 + c2*t, sin(t)) suggests changing environment (e.g., climate change or seasonal forcing).
- Removal/harvesting signature → subtraction of a term independent of P or a saturating rational term P/(c+P) points to human exploitation or predation pressure.
- Logarithmic dependence → log(P) appearing in dP/dt (e.g., P*log(P)) is characteristic of Gompertz-type growth, producing a slower approach to carrying capacity.
- Allometric scaling → terms like P^c (c not 1) without a logistic cap are typical of von Bertalanffy or generalized metabolic growth models.
- Multiple equilibria → cubic or higher-order polynomials in P on the right-hand side produce multiple fixed points, including threshold populations (Allee effect).

- Second term: `0.9198*P²/(7.531*P + 1)`

So GT = `c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P²/(c_d*P + 1)` where c_a ≈ -0.01095, c_b ≈ 0.9198

Equivalently: **GT = αP² + βP + γP²/(δP + 1)**

Now I can rewrite the rational term: `γP²/(δP + 1) = γP·P/(δP + 1)`. Note that `P²/(δP+1)` can also be written as `P/(δ) - P/(δ²) + P/(δ²(δP+1))` via polynomial division... but let me think more carefully.

Actually, `P²/(δP + 1)` = `P/δ - 1/δ² + 1/(δ²(δP+1))`. So:

GT = αP² + βP + γ[P/δ - 1/δ² + 1/(δ²(δP+1))]
   = αP² + (β + γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))

Alternatively, the GT structure is: **P² term + P term + P²/(linear in P)**

Note that `P²/(δP + 1)` can be rewritten. Let me check: `P·P/(δP+1) = P·[1/δ - 1/(δ(δP+1))] = P/δ - P/(δ(δP+1))`

So `P²/(δP+1) = P/δ - P/(δ(δP+1))`. And `P/(δP+1) = 1/δ - 1/(δ(δP+1))`.

This means: `γP²/(δP+1) = (γ/δ)P - (γ/δ)·P/(δP+1)`

So GT = αP² + βP + (γ/δ)P - (γ/δ)·P/(δP+1)
     = αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - (γ/δ)·P/(δP+1)

Now `P/(δP+1)` with substitution `c₃ = 1/δ` becomes `P/(P + 1/δ)` times `1/δ`... Let me be more careful.

`P/(δP+1)` = `(1/δ)·P/(P + 1/δ)` = `(1/δ)·[1 - (1/δ)/(P + 1/δ)]` = `1/δ - 1/(δ²(P + 1/δ))`... Hmm, let me just keep the GT in its natural form:

**GT = aP² + bP + cP²/(dP + e)** where a, b, c, d, e are specific constants.

This can also be written as: **aP² + bP + (c/d)·P·[P/(P + e/d)]**

Or equivalently: **aP² + bP + c'·P/(P + f)** where the rational part is `P/(P+f)` NOT `P²/(P+f)`.

Wait, let me recheck. The GT second term is `0.9198*P²/(7.531P + 1)`. This is `P²/(linear)`, not `P/(linear)`.

Let me see which candidates can match the form `αP² + βP + γP²/(δP + ε)`.

Note: `P²/(δP + ε) = (1/δ)·P - (ε/δ²) + (ε²/δ²)·1/(δP+ε)` by polynomial long division.

Also: `P²/(δP + ε) = P·[P/(δP+ε)]`. And `P/(δP+ε)` is a different basis than `P/(P+c)` only by scaling.

The key structural elements of GT (independent of `t`):
1. A `P²` term
2. A `P` term  
3. A `P²/(linear in P)` term (equivalently expressible as combinations of P, constant, and 1/(linear in P))

(b) Its `P`-dependent structure matches

For candidates with `t`-dependent terms, I can set coefficients to zero to eliminate them.

For candidates that are purely `P`-dependent, I need to check structural equivalence.

Let me go through systematically:

**Candidate 1:** `P²c0 + P²c1/(c2 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5)) + Pc6 + Pc7/(P + c8)`

Has `t`-dependence in `P²c1/(c2 + c3*sin(c4*t+c5))`. Setting c1=0 eliminates it: `P²c0 + Pc6 + Pc7/(P+c8)`. This gives `P² + P + P/(P+c)`. But GT needs `P²/(P+c)` not `P/(P+c)`. These are different rational functions. `P/(P+c)` approaches 1 as P→∞, while `P²/(P+c)` approaches P. So this cannot match.

Wait - can I combine terms? `P²c0 + Pc7/(P+c8)`. The `P²` term plus `P/(P+c)` gives behavior like `c0*P² + c7*(1 - c8/(P+c8))` = `c0*P² + c7 - c7*c8/(P+c8)`. The GT has `P²/(P+c)` which behaves like `P/c` for large P. So the structures don't match.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3) + c4*log(Pc5+1)*sin(c6t+c7)`

Set c4=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3)`. Same issue - has `P/(P+c)` not `P²/(P+c)`.

Wait, but can `P²c0 + Pc2/(P+c3)` match `αP² + βP + γP²/(δP+1)`? Let me check if `Pc2/(P+c3)` can somehow produce a `P²/(P+c)` term.

`P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3)` - combining over common denominator `(P+c3)`:
= `[c0*P²(P+c3) + c1*P(P+c3) + c2*P] / (P+c3)`
= `[c0*P³ + c0*c3*P² + c1*P² + c1*c3*P + c2*P] / (P+c3)`

GT over common denominator `(δP+1)`:
= `[αP²(δP+1) + βP(δP+1) + γP²] / (δP+1)`
= `[αδP³ + αP² + βδP² + βP + γP²] / (δP+1)`
= `[αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP] / (δP+1)`

For candidate: numerator = `c0*P³ + (c0c3+c1)P² + (c1c3+c2)P`, denominator = `P+c3`
For GT: numerator = `αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP`, denominator = `δP+1`

For these to be equal: the ratio of denominators must equal the ratio of numerators.

`(P+c3)/(δP+1)` must be constant (since both are degree 1). This means `c3 = 1/δ` and the constant ratio is `1/δ`.

Then numerator_candidate = (1/δ) * numerator_GT:
- `c0 = αδ/δ = α` ✓ (just set c0)
- `c0c3 + c1 = (α+βδ+γ)/δ` → `c0/δ + c1 = α/δ + β + γ/δ` → `c1 = β + γ/δ`
- `c1c3 + c2 = β/δ` → `(β+γ/δ)/δ + c2 = β/δ` → `β/δ + γ/δ² + c2 = β/δ` → `c2 = -γ/δ²`

So yes! The candidate `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3)` CAN match the GT!

Let me verify with actual numbers:
- α = -0.01095, β = 0.9198, γ = 0.9198, δ = 7.531, ε = 1

c0 = α = -0.01095
c3 = 1/δ = 1/7.531 ≈ 0.1328
c1 = β + γ/δ = 0.9198 + 0.9198/7.531 = 0.9198 + 0.1221 = 1.0419
c2 = -γ/δ² = -0.9198/56.72 = -0.01621

Let me verify: `c0P² + c1P + c2P/(P+c3)`
= `-0.01095P² + 1.0419P - 0.01621P/(P + 0.1328)`

Combine: common denominator (P + 0.1328):
= `[-0.01095P²(P+0.1328) + 1.0419P(P+0.1328) - 0.01621P] / (P+0.1328)`

Numerator:
= `-0.01095P³ - 0.001454P² + 1.0419P² + 0.13836P - 0.01621P`
= `-0.01095P³ + 1.04045P² + 0.12215P`

GT numerator over (δP+1):
= `αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP`
= `-0.01095*7.531*P³ + (-0.01095 + 0.9198*7.531 + 0.9198)P² + 0.9198P`
= `-0.08246P³ + (−0.01095 + 6.9264 + 0.9198)P² + 0.9198P`
= `-0.08246P³ + 7.8353P² + 0.9198P`

GT denominator: 7.531P + 1

Candidate denominator: P + 0.1328

Ratio of denominators: (7.531P+1)/(P+0.1328) = 7.531 (if 1/0.1328 ≈ 7.531, which is 1/0.13278 = 7.531 ✓)

So candidate numerator should be GT numerator / 7.531:
= `-0.08246/7.531 P³ + 7.8353/7.531 P² + 0.9198/7.531 P`
= `-0.01095P³ + 1.04045P² + 0.12215P` ✓

This matches! So Candidate 2 (with c4=0) matches GT.

Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3) + Pc4*sin(c5t+c6)`

Set c4=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(P+c3)`. Same as Candidate 2's core. 

Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 4:** `P²c0 + P²c1*sin(c2t+c3) + Pc4 + Pc5/(P+c6)`

Set c1=0: `P²c0 + Pc4 + Pc5/(P+c6)`. Same structure as above.

Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(Pc3+c4) + c5*sin(c6t+c7) + c8/(Pc3+c4)`

Set c5=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(Pc3+c4) + c8/(Pc3+c4)` = `P²c0 + Pc1 + (Pc2+c8)/(Pc3+c4)`

The rational part is `(c2P + c8)/(c3P + c4)`. This approaches `c2/c3` as P→∞, which is a constant. But GT's rational part `P²/(δP+1)` grows like P. So can the combination work?

Actually, let me reconsider. The full expression is `P²c0 + Pc1 + (c2P+c8)/(c3P+c4)`.

From the analysis above, we need `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(Pc3+c4)` to match, plus the extra `c8/(Pc3+c4)`.

The GT, when expressed over denominator (δP+1), has no constant term in P (the numerator has P³, P², P but no constant). Let me check if adding `c8/(c3P+c4)` breaks things.

GT = `P²α + Pβ + P²γ/(δP+1)`. Over common denominator (δP+1):
Numerator = `αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP`

Candidate over common denominator (c3P+c4):
= `c0P²(c3P+c4) + c1P(c3P+c4) + c2P + c8`
= `c0c3P³ + (c0c4+c1c3)P² + (c1c4+c2)P + c8`

For GT: no constant term in numerator. So we need c8 = 0 (since the denominators are proportional, the numerators must be proportional too, and GT numerator has no constant term).

But wait, c8 is a free constant, so setting c8=0 is allowed! Then it reduces to the same form.

Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]

The `sin(Pc6+c7)` term depends on P, not just t. Setting c5=0 eliminates it. Then: `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(Pc3+c4) + c8/(Pc3+c4)`. Set c8=0: same core form `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2/(Pc3+c4)` which is equivalent to `P²c0 + Pc1 + Pc2'/(P+c3')`.

The `tanh` term is a different basis function from anything in GT. Setting c2=0 and c5=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + c8/(Pc6+c7)`. This has `1/(linear P)` but GT needs `P/(linear P)` or `P²/(linear P)`. The `1/(linear P)` term approaches 0 as P→∞, while `P²/(linear P)` approaches P/δ. So we can't match unless c8=0, giving just `P²c0 + Pc1`, which is missing the rational term.

**Candidate 14:** `P²c0 + Pc1 + c2*exp(Pc3) + c4*t/(Pc5+c6) + c7/(Pc5+c6)`

The `exp(Pc3)` term: if c3≠0, this is an exponential in P which can't match any polynomial/rational structure. Setting c2=0 and c4=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + c7/(Pc5+c6)`. This has `1/(linear P)` but not `P/(linear P)`. Setting c7=0 too: just `P²c0 + Pc1`, missing the rational term.

Can I set c3=0? Then `c2*exp(0) = c2`, a constant. So: `P²c0 + Pc1 + c2 + c7/(Pc5+c6)`. Still `1/(linear P)` not `P/(linear P)`.

Hmm, but from the GT analysis, `P²/(δP+1)` can be decomposed as `P/δ - 1/δ² + 1/(δ²(δP+1))`. So GT = `αP² + βP + γ/δ·P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))` = `αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))`.

So GT = `P² term + P term + constant + 1/(linear P)`.

With c3=0: `P²c0 + Pc1 + c2 + c7/(Pc5+c6)`. This has exactly those four components! Let me check:
- c0 = α
- c1 = β + γ/δ  
- c2 = -γ/δ²
- c7/(c5P + c6) = γ/(δ²(δP+1))

So c5 = δ, c6 = 1, c7 = γ/δ² · 1 ... wait: c7/(c5P+c6) = γ/(δ²·(δP+1)). So c7 = γ/δ², c5 = δ, c6 = 1. And c4=0 to eliminate t.

Yes! This works!

Candidate 14 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 17:** `Pc0/(P+c1) + Pc2*(c3+t)^c4 + P^c5*c6`

Set c2=0: `Pc0/(P+c1) + P^c5*c6`. 

Can `P^c5*c6` provide both `P²` and `P` terms? No, it's a single power of P. So we'd need c5=2 giving `P²c6 + Pc0/(P+c1)`. This is `P² + P/(P+c)` which from our analysis can match `P² + P + P²/(P+c)` structure? Let me check.

GT = `αP² + βP + γP²/(δP+1)`. Can this equal `c6P² + c0P/(P+c1)`?

Over common denominator (P+c1):
Candidate: `c6P²(P+c1) + c0P` = `c6P³ + c6c1P² + c0P`

GT over (δP+1): `αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP`

Ratio of denominators: (P+c1)/(δP+1). For this to be constant, c1 = 1/δ, ratio = 1/δ.

Candidate numerator = GT numerator / δ:
- `c6 = αδ/δ = α`
- `c6c1 = (α+βδ+γ)/δ` → `α/δ = α/δ + β + γ/δ` → `0 = β + γ/δ`

But β = 0.9198 and γ/δ = 0.9198/7.531 ≈ 0.1221. So β + γ/δ ≈ 1.042 ≠ 0.

So this doesn't work with c2=0. What about keeping c2? `Pc2*(c3+t)^c4` - if c4=0, this becomes `Pc2*1 = c2P`. Then: `Pc0/(P+c1) + c2P + c6P^c5`.

With c5=2: `c6P² + c2P + c0P/(P+c1)`. This is `P² + P + P/(P+c)` which is the same core structure! Match.

`P*P^c0*c1/(P+c2) + Pc3/(P+c2) + Pc4*log(Pc5+1)/(P+c2) + P^c0*c6/(P+c2) + c7*log(Pc5+1)/(P+c2)`

**Candidate 37:** `Pc0/(P+c1) + Pc2 + P^c3*c4 + c5`

With c3=2: `c4P² + c2P + c0P/(P+c1) + c5`.

GT = `αP² + βP + γP²/(δP+1)`. From the decomposition: GT = `αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))`.

Candidate: `c4P² + c2P + c0P/(P+c1) + c5`.

`c0P/(P+c1) = c0 - c0c1/(P+c1)`.

So candidate = `c4P² + c2P + c0 + c5 - c0c1/(P+c1)` = `c4P² + c2P + (c0+c5) - c0c1/(P+c1)`.

GT = `αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))`.

Matching:
- c4 = α ✓
- c2 = β+γ/δ ✓
- c0+c5 = -γ/δ² ✓
- -c0c1/(P+c1) = γ/(δ²(δP+1))

For the last: -c0c1/(P+c1) = γ/(δ²(δP+1)). 

Let c1 = 1/δ. Then: -c0/(δ(P+1/δ)) = -c0δ/(δ²(δP+1)) = -c0/(δ(δP+1)).

Wait: -c0c1/(P+c1) with c1=1/δ: = -c0·(1/δ)/(P+1/δ) = -c0/(δP+1).

We need this to equal γ/(δ²(δP+1)). So: -c0 = γ/δ². Thus c0 = -γ/δ².

Then c5 = -γ/δ² - c0 = -γ/δ² - (-γ/δ²) = 0. Fine.

Check c2: need c2 = β + γ/δ. Independent of c0. ✓

So: c4=α, c2=β+γ/δ, c0=-γ/δ², c1=1/δ, c3=2, c5=0. All valid!

Candidate 37 verdict: [MATCH]

Two `P/(linear P)` terms. `P/(P+c1)` and `P/(c3P+c4)` are both of the form `P/(linear P)`. These are not independent - `P/(c3P+c4) = (1/c3)·P/(P+c4/c3)`.

If c1 = c4/c3, these combine: `c6P² + (c0+c2/c3)P/(P+c1)`. This is `P² + P/(P+c)` which is the core structure. Match.

Even if c1 ≠ c4/c3, we can set c2=0: `c6P² + c0P/(P+c1)`. Then we need a P term... we don't have one explicitly. But `c0P/(P+c1) = c0 - c0c1/(P+c1)`. So candidate = `c6P² + c0 - c0c1/(P+c1)`. This doesn't have a standalone P term.

Hmm, but with both rational terms: `c0P/(P+c1) + (c2/c3)P/(P+c4/c3)`. If c1 ≠ c4/c3, these are two independent `P/(P+a)` terms. Each `P/(P+a) = 1 - a/(P+a)`. So sum = `(c0+c2/c3) - c0c1/(P+c1) - (c2c4/c3²)/(P+c4/c3)`.

GT decomposed: `αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))`.

The candidate has `P²` and two `1/(P+a)` terms but no `P` term. Two `1/(P+a)` terms with different `a` values cannot produce a `P` term. So this doesn't work unless we can get a P term.

Actually wait, I was wrong. Let me reconsider. The candidate is `c6P² + c0P/(P+c1) + c2P/(c3P+c4)`. Let me combine everything over a common denominator `(P+c1)(c3P+c4)`:

Numerator = `c6P²(P+c1)(c3P+c4) + c0P(c3P+c4) + c2P(P+c1)`

This is a degree 4 polynomial in P over a degree 2 polynomial. GT is degree 3 over degree 1. These can potentially match if the degree 4 and degree 2 terms factor appropriately.

Actually, this is getting complicated. Let me just use the simpler approach: set c1 = c4/c3 so both rational terms share the same denominator. Then it works as shown above. But we need a P term.

`c6P² + (c0 + c2/c3)P/(P + c1)`. Decompose: `c6P² + (c0+c2/c3) - (c0+c2/c3)c1/(P+c1)`.

GT: `αP² + (β+γ/δ)P - γ/δ² + γ/(δ²(δP+1))`.

The candidate has no P term but GT does. So this doesn't match.

What if c1 ≠ c4/c3? Let me try a different approach. Over common denominator (P+c1)(c3P+c4):

GT: `[αδP³ + (α+βδ+γ)P² + βP] · (denominator ratio)`

The candidate has a P⁴ term which GT doesn't. So c6c3=0. If c6=0, no P² term. If c3=0: `c2P/(c4)` = constant·P, and candidate = `c6P² + c0P/(P+c1) + (c2/c4)P`. This is `P² + P + P/(P+c)`. Match!

So with c3=0: candidate = `c6P² + c0P/(P+c1) + (c2/c4)P + c7/c4`. Set c7=0. Then `c6P² + (c2/c4)P + c0P/(P+c1)`. Same core!
